---

### **Mac Not Recognizing SD Card? Try This:**

1. **Basic Checks First**
   - Is the SD card properly inserted (flush, no wiggle)?
   - Try removing and reinserting it slowly.

2. **Finder Preferences**
   - Open **Finder > Settings > General**
   - Make sure **â€œExternal disksâ€** is checked to show on the desktop.

3. **Disk Utility**
   - Open **Disk Utility** (Spotlight search it)
   - See if the SD card shows up there (even if grayed out).
   - If itâ€™s there, try clicking **Mount**.

4. **Reboot with Card Inserted**
   - Sometimes a restart with the card already in the slot works.

5. **Try a Different Adapter**
   - If you're using a USB/SD dongle, try another port or dongle. Faulty adapters are a common culprit.

The MPC **can read and play MP3 files**, but:

- **MP3s take longer to load** because they must be decoded in real time.
- **They do not stretch or time warp cleanly** like WAV files do.
- **Audio editing (chop, reverse, pitch shift)** is far more stable and accurate with WAV.

---

### **Recommendation:**
**Always convert your stems and track sources to 16-bit or 24-bit WAV** (44.1 kHz or 48 kHz) before importing into your MPC.

Hereâ€™s your ideal setup:

```plaintext
/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish.wav        â† Main track (instrumental or full)
+ optional:
/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish_hook.wav  â† Isolated stems
/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish_verse1.wav
```

MP3s are fine for reference listening or placeholder clips,  
but when youâ€™re slicing, mixing, or resampling: **WAV is king**.

Want me to help you set up a quick drag-and-drop MP3 to WAV conversion station on the Mac later?

While the MPC doesnâ€™t have a â€œmagic stem splitterâ€ built-in like iZotope or Spleeter, the latest versions *do* give you a powerful workaround using **Audio Tracks + Slice + Resample** to manually stem and layer.

Letâ€™s walk through the most effective way to extract vocals/instrumentals **inside MPC Standalone**, step by step:

---

## **Method: Manual Stem Isolation Using Duplicate Audio Tracks**

This doesnâ€™t â€œripâ€ stems like AI separation, but it allows for **layer manipulation**â€”such as vocal-only passes, chopping instrumental sections, or creating acapella-style arrangements.

---

### **1. Duplicate the Full Audio Track**
- On the **Main screen**, select your full-length audio track (e.g., Audio 001).
- Tap the **pencil icon** and choose **Duplicate Track**.
- Now you have two identical audio tracks, stacked.

Rename one:
- `Instrumental Layer`
- The other: `Vocal Layer`

This gives you freedom to edit them separately.

---

### **2. EQ Filter (Fake Stem Method)**
On each track, apply an EQ to isolate what you want:

- **For Instrumental:**
  - Add **high-pass + low-pass filters** to remove vocal mids
  - Use Parametric EQ to reduce vocal frequency range (usually 1kHzâ€“5kHz)

- **For Vocal:**
  - Do the oppositeâ€”cut lows/highs, boost mids slightly
  - Youâ€™ll get a **quasi-acapella** effect

**This isnâ€™t perfect**, but it can simulate stem separation enough to:
- Layer your own beat underneath
- Mute one and re-record over it
- Use for timing + alignment before doing a â€œrealâ€ AI separation on Mac

---

### **3. (Optional) Slice Tool for Section-Based â€œStemsâ€**
- Open the `Sample Edit` screen
- Use **Regions** or **Threshold-based Slicing**
- Isolate verses, hooks, bridge manually
- Assign those to different pads or tracks to manipulate independently

---

### **4. Resample Your Results**
Once you EQ and isolate:

- Create a new audio track
- Solo the EQâ€™d track
- Use **Resample** function (from menu) to bounce a new WAV of just that layer
- Now youâ€™ve got a usable â€œstemâ€ saved in-project

---

### Alternative: Use Studio One for True AI Stem Separation
If you want clean stems (vocals vs. instruments), export the full track to your Mac and run it through:
- **LALAL.AI**
- **Splitter.ai**
- **RX 10 Music Rebalance**
- Or even **Studio Oneâ€™s built-in tools**

Then bounce the clean stems back to your MPC.

So:

```plaintext
Total seconds = 8,193,983 / 44,100 â‰ˆ 185.79 seconds
```

### Step 2: Seconds to Bars

Youâ€™re working at **84.55 BPM**, which means each beat lasts:

```plaintext

```

There are **4 beats per bar**, so:

```plaintext
One bar = 0.7095 * 4 â‰ˆ 2.838 seconds per bar
```

Then:

```plaintext
185.79 seconds / 2.838 seconds per bar â‰ˆ 65.5 bars
```

---

### Final Answer:

**The track "Swordfish" is approximately 66 bars long at 84.55 BPM.**
